=041  \\$ager
=245  00$a"Mater celeberr. Mozart":$cAnna Maria Mozart zum 300. Geburtstag
=246  30$aAnna Maria Mozart zum 300. Geburtstag
=260  \\$aVienna$bHollitzer$c2023
=300  \\$a233 pages$b23 illustrations
=490  0\$aSchriftenreihe des Archivs der Erzdiözese Salzburg$v27
=504  \\$aIncludes bibliographical references (pages 200--225) and index.
=520  \\$aMaria Anna Mozart, the mother of the Mozart siblings and wife of Leopold Mozart, is often described as uneducated, unsociable and not even musical. Many biographers of Wolfgang Amadé Mozart agree that he inherited his talent from his father and his tendency to use faecal language from his mother.

To mark the 300th anniversary of her birth, Anna Maria Mozart, née Pertl (1720-1778) is at the centre of a new book for the first time. Published by Hollitzer-Verlag in Vienna, the symposium volume mater celeberr. Mozart. Anna Maria Mozart on her 300th birthday, edited by Anja Morgenstern and Eva Neumayr, contributions by Mirijam Beier, Christoph Großpietsch, Monika Kammerlander, Anja Morgenstern, Eva Neumayr, Wolfgang Neuper and Käthe Springer-Dissman deal with her biography, her education, her depiction in pictures and her reception in the Mozart biography of the mother of the Mozart siblings.
In addition, the important social role of musicians‘ mothers in the 18th century will be discussed on the basis of selected biographies that shed light on the cultural activities of women in musicians’ families, thereby also revealing new aspects of Anna Maria Mozart's life and work. The results presented here suggest that Anna Maria Mozart had a stronger influence on the development of her famous son Wolfgang Amadé than previously assumed.

=245  10$aFrauen als Komponistinnen im Umfeld Mozarts:$bmit einem besonderen Augenmerk auf Maria Theresia Paradis
=260  \\$aMunich$bAVM Press$c2018
=300  \\$a86 pages
=504  \\$aIncludes bibliographical references (pages 71-75).
=505  0\$aDie Frau in 18. Jahrhundert -- Frauen als Komponistinnen im Unfeld W.A. Mozarts. Nannerl, als Schwester im Schatten des grossen Komponisten (1751-1829) ; Komponistionsschülerinnen von Mozart : die Tochter des Comte de Guines, Josepha Auernhammer und Babette Ployer (?) ; Komponieren als Zeitvertreb für Frauen in besonderen Berufe ; Nannette Streicher, née Stein, die Klavierbauerin (1769-1833) ; Franziska Danzi-Lebrun, die Sängerin (1756-1791) ; Komponieren als Beruf(ung) ; Josepha Auernhammer, Mozarts Schülerin (1758-1820) ; Marianna Martines (1744-1812) ; Maria Theresia Paradis (1759-1824), blinde Pianistin, Komponistin und Lehrerin -- Conclusio.
=520  8\$aEven if their names are almost forgotten, female composers made a significant contribution to cultural and musical life in Mozart's time. Maria Theresia Paradis, Marianne Martines, Josepha Auernhammer, Nanette Streicher, Franziska Lebrun-Danzi, Babette Ployer and Mozart's sister Nannerl are considered to be the most important representatives. Many of their works have not survived and the few that are known have been attributed to male composers for many years. Being a female musician and especially a female composer was difficult. It is no coincidence that Maria Theresia Paradis said: ‘Would my male colleagues in the arts forgive me if I dared to compete with them as a woman - even as a faceless woman?’ It was not easy to assert themselves and yet female composers were recognised by the public and could point to many successes. This book explores the question of the extent to which it was possible for a woman to hold her own alongside her male colleagues in Mozart's time. (Translated with Deepl.com)

=100  \\$aAristoteles$d384-322 BC$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q868$94906
=245  \\$aThe Rhetoric of Aristotle,$bwith an commentary by the late Edward Meredith Cope ... revised and edited for the syndics of the University press by John Edwin Sandys
=260  \\$aCambridge$bCambridge University Press$c1877
=300  \\$a3 vols. (xx-302+[viii]-340+]viii]-270 pages)
=520  \\$aEdward Meredith Cope was an English scholar of classics who served as Fellow and Tutor at Trinity College, Cambridge. One of the leading Greek specialists of his time, Cope published An Introduction to Aristotle's Rhetoric in 1867. Though now considered a 'standard work', that Introduction was intended as merely the first part of a full critical edition of the Rhetoric, which was left incomplete on Cope's death in 1873. Cope's manuscripts were collected and edited by John Edwin Sandys, and published in this three-volume set in 1877. Cope's analysis represented an important advance in the modern interpretation of this foundational text on the art of persuasion. Volume 1 contains the Greek text of Book 1 together with a commentary on Aristotle's introduction to his topic and his definition of rhetoric and its subdivisions. Volume 2 contains the Greek text of Book 2 together with a commentary on Aristotle's views concerning the place of emotion and logic within the discipline. Volume 3 contains the Greek text of Book 3 together with a commentary on Aristotle's understanding of style, arrangement and other rhetorical devices.
